
<span id="page-63-1"></span><span id="page-63-0"></span>**Fig. 21.** Hybrid games for SC-aCCA security. We denote by  $h \in \mathcal{HK}$  the base vector for kernel space corresponds to the dimension k linear language with support in  $\mathbb{F}^{\ell}$ . Note that such vector can be generated together with the linear language.

<u>Game  $G_3$ :</u> The only difference between  $G_3$  and  $G_2$  is that, the challenge ciphertext is encrypted using the hash key hk instead of using the public key projk. We generate the challenge ciphertext as

```
\mathsf{ct}_0 \overset{\hspace{0.1em}\mathsf{\scriptscriptstyle\$}}{\leftarrow} \mathsf{Sample}_{\mathcal{L}}(\mathsf{lpk}) \quad \mathsf{ct}_1 := \mathsf{SEval}(\mathsf{hk}_i' + \mathsf{hk}, \mathsf{ct}_0) \quad \mathsf{ct}_2 := \mathsf{SEval}(\mathsf{hk}, \mathsf{ct}_0) + \mathsf{m}_b
```

{64}------------------------------------------------

since  $\mathsf{ct}_0 \in \mathcal{L}_{\mathsf{lpk}}$  with witness w, by the perfect correctness of HPS, the challenge ciphertext in  $\mathbf{G}_3$  and  $\mathbf{G}_2$  is identical. Therefore, we have

$$pr_3 = pr_2$$
.

Game  $G_4$ : In this game, we change the way of generating the zero-knowledge proof  $\pi^*$  in the challenge ciphertext. Instead of generating  $\pi^*$  using the witness w of  $ct_0$ , we generate  $\pi^*$  using the simulation trapdoor simK. By the zero-knowledge property of the proof system, we have

$$|\mathsf{pr}_4 - \mathsf{pr}_3| \leq \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathsf{tLM-NIZK},\mathcal{B}}^{\mathsf{ZK}}(1^{\lambda}).$$

Game  $G_5$ : In this game, we introduce a list  $\mathcal{L}_t$  in  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{Chall}}$  to store the Tag of the challenge ciphertexts, then we reject any decryption query that uses the same tag as the challenge ciphertext. Let  $\mathsf{Bad}_{\mathsf{Tag}}$  be the event that the adversary submits a decryption query with the challenge tag that would otherwise be accepted by the decryption oracle. If  $\mathsf{Bad}_{\mathsf{Tag}}$  occurs, the game aborts. As in the general construction, this bad event occurs with probability at most  $\mathsf{Adv}^{\mathsf{StUnforg}}_{\mathsf{OTS},\mathcal{B}}(1^{\lambda}) + \mathsf{Adv}^{\mathsf{Collision}}_{\mathsf{H},\mathcal{B}}(1^{\lambda}) + \mathsf{Adv}^{\mathsf{SSS}}_{\mathsf{tLM-NIZK},\mathcal{B}}(1^{\lambda})$ . Thus, we have

$$|\mathsf{pr}_5 - \mathsf{pr}_4| \leq \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathsf{OTS},\mathcal{B}}^{\mathsf{StUnforg}}(1^\lambda) + \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathsf{H},\mathcal{B}}^{\mathsf{Collision}}(1^\lambda) + \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathsf{tLM-NIZK},\mathcal{B}}^{\mathsf{SSS}}(1^\lambda).$$

Game  $G_6$ : In this game, we reject any re-encryption query that  $ct_0$  is not sampled from the  $\mathcal{L}_{lpk}$  with witness w or  $ct_1$  is not computed as  $ct_1 := \mathsf{PEval}(\mathsf{projk}_i, ct_0, \mathsf{w})$ . Since the challenger knows the trapdoor td, it can always check the validity of the re-encryption queries. Let  $\mathsf{Bad}_{\mathsf{ReEnc}}$  be the event that the adversary submits a re-encryption query that would otherwise be accepted by the re-encryption oracle. If  $\mathsf{Bad}_{\mathsf{ReEnc}}$  occurs, the game aborts. By the special simulation-soundness of the proof system, we have

$$|\mathsf{pr}_6 - \mathsf{pr}_5| \leq \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathsf{tLM-NIZK},\mathcal{B}}^{\mathsf{SSS}}(1^{\lambda}).$$

Game  $G_7$ : In this game, we change the way the challenge ciphertext is generated. Instead of sampling  $\mathsf{ct}_0$  from the language using  $\mathsf{Sample}_{\mathcal{L}}(\mathsf{lpk})$ , we sample it from the statement set  $\mathsf{ct}_0 \overset{\hspace{0.1em}\mathsf{\scriptscriptstyle\$}}{\leftarrow} \mathsf{Sample}_{\mathcal{X}}(1^\lambda)$ . Since the bad event  $\mathsf{Bad}_{\mathsf{Col}}$  does not occur, the adversary cannot simply check if  $\mathsf{ct}_0 \in \mathcal{L}_{\mathsf{lpk}}$  by checking if  $\mathsf{SEval}(\mathsf{hk}_i - \mathsf{hk}_j, \mathsf{ct}_0) = 0$  where i, j are any two collision users. <sup>22</sup> By the hard subset membership property of the language, we have

$$|\mathsf{pr}_7 - \mathsf{pr}_6| \leq \mathsf{Adv}^{\mathsf{HSM}}_{\mathsf{SMP},\mathcal{B}}(1^{\lambda}).$$

<span id="page-64-0"></span>If there is a collision between two public keys  $\mathsf{pk}_i$  and  $\mathsf{pk}_j$ , then the adversary can simply gets  $\mathsf{hk}_i - \mathsf{hk}_j \in \mathcal{HK}''$  by querying the oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{CorrT}}(i,j)$ , and check if  $\mathsf{SEval}(\mathsf{hk}_i - \mathsf{hk}_j, \mathsf{ct}_0) = 0$ . If yes, then  $\mathsf{ct}_0 \in \mathcal{L}_{\mathsf{lpk}}$ , otherwise  $\mathsf{ct}_0 \notin \mathcal{L}_{\mathsf{lpk}}$ .

{65}------------------------------------------------

<u>Game G<sub>8</sub></u>: In  $G_8$ , we introduce a bad event  $Bad_{Univ}$  that captures the failure of the universal hash property. Specifically, we define

$$\mathsf{Bad}_{\mathsf{Univ}} \coloneqq \{ \forall \mathsf{hk}'' \in \mathcal{HK}'' : \mathsf{SEval}(\mathsf{hk}'', \mathsf{x}) = 0 \mid \mathsf{ct}_0 \xleftarrow{\$} \mathsf{U}(\mathcal{X}) \}.$$

We recall that  $\mathcal{HK}' \subset \mathcal{HK}$  is the affine vector space, such that we can change hk to any element  $hk' \in \mathcal{HK}'$  without changing its projection over  $\mathcal{L}_{lpk}$ .  $\mathcal{HK}''$  is the vector space that corresponds to the affine vector space  $\mathcal{HK}'$ . Using the universality of VSHPS, we have

$$|\mathsf{pr}_8 - \mathsf{pr}_7| \leq \Pr[\mathsf{Bad}_{\mathsf{Univ}}] \leq \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathsf{VSHPS},\mathcal{B}}^{\mathsf{Bad}\mathsf{Univ}}(1^{\lambda}).$$

Game  $G_9$ : In this game, we modify the generation of the challenge ciphertext. We sample  $v \leftarrow U(\mathbb{F})$  at the beginning of the experiment and compute the challenge ciphertext as  $\mathsf{ct}_1 := \mathsf{SEval}(\mathsf{hk}_i, \mathsf{ct}_0) + v \cdot \mathsf{SEval}(\mathsf{h}, \mathsf{ct}_0) + \mathsf{SEval}(\mathsf{hk}, \mathsf{ct}_0)$  where  $\mathsf{h}$  is a basis of the  $\mathcal{HK}''$  over the linear language  $\mathcal{L}_{\mathsf{lpk}}$ .

Since the game does not abort, we are guaranteed that  $\mathsf{SEval}(\mathsf{h}, \mathsf{ct}_0) \neq 0$ . As v is chosen uniformly at random from  $\mathbb{F}$ , the term  $v \cdot \mathsf{SEval}(\mathsf{h}, \mathsf{ct}_0)$  acts as a one-time pad, perfectly masking the ciphertext component. Thus, we can also modify  $\mathsf{ct}_1$  to be  $\mathsf{ct}_1 \leftarrow \mathsf{U}(\mathbb{F})$  without changing the adversary's view.

We first give the value of  $|pr_9 - pr_8|$ , then we explain why the above modification is valid in Lemma 5. We have

$$|\mathsf{pr}_9 - \mathsf{pr}_8| = 0.$$

**Game G**<sub>10</sub>: In this game, we modify the generation of the challenge ciphertext. We sample  $v' \leftarrow U(\mathbb{F})$  at the beginning of the experiment and compute the challenge ciphertext as  $\mathsf{ct}_2 := \mathsf{SEval}(\mathsf{hk}, \mathsf{ct}_0) + v' \cdot \mathsf{SEval}(\mathsf{h}, \mathsf{ct}_0) + \mathsf{m}$ .

The proof process is similar to that of  $G_9$ , we first translate hk to hk +  $v' \cdot h$ , then delete all the  $v' \cdot h$  components from other oracle except  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{Chall}}$ . Since hk is independent with re-encryption keys  $\mathsf{d}_{i,j}$ , we can do this without considering a selective adversary first, which means S2A lemma is not need. Above all, we have

$$|\mathsf{pr}_{10} - \mathsf{pr}_9| = 0.$$

Finally, we observe that in  $G_9$ , the challenge ciphertext is computed as

$$\begin{split} \mathsf{ct}_0 & \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathsf{Sample}_{\mathcal{X}}(1^{\lambda}) \\ \mathsf{ct}_1 &:= \mathsf{SEval}(\mathsf{hk}_1 + \mathsf{hk}, \mathsf{ct}_0) + v \cdot \mathsf{SEval}(\mathsf{h}, \mathsf{ct}_0) \\ \mathsf{ct}_2 &:= \mathsf{SEval}(\mathsf{hk}, \mathsf{ct}_0) + v' \cdot \mathsf{SEval}(\mathsf{h}, \mathsf{ct}_0) + \mathsf{m}_b \end{split}$$

Since v' is chosen uniformly at random from  $\mathbb{F}$  and  $\mathsf{SEval}(\mathsf{h},\mathsf{ct}_0) \neq 0$ , the term  $v' \cdot \mathsf{SEval}(\mathsf{h},\mathsf{ct}_0)$  acts as a one-time pad, perfectly masking the message  $\mathsf{m}_b$ . Therefore, the adversary's success probability is exactly 1/2, and we have

$$\operatorname{pr}_9 = \frac{1}{2}.$$

{66}------------------------------------------------

Taking union bound over all the hybrid games, we have

$$\begin{split} \mathsf{Adv}^{\mathsf{SC-aHRA}}_{\mathsf{PRE},\mathcal{A}}(\lambda) \leq & \binom{\mathsf{N_U}}{2} \cdot \mathsf{Adv}^{\mathsf{KCol}}_{\mathsf{SMP},\mathcal{B}}(1^\lambda) + \mathsf{Adv}^{\mathsf{ZK}}_{\mathsf{tLM-NIZK},\mathcal{B}}(1^\lambda) + \mathsf{Adv}^{\mathsf{StUnforg}}_{\mathsf{OTS},\mathcal{B}}(1^\lambda) \\ & + \mathsf{Adv}^{\mathsf{Collision}}_{\mathsf{H},\mathcal{B}}(1^\lambda) + 2 \cdot \mathsf{Adv}^{\mathsf{SSS}}_{\mathsf{tLM-NIZK},\mathcal{B}}(1^\lambda) + \mathsf{Adv}^{\mathsf{HSM}}_{\mathsf{SMP},\mathcal{B}}(1^\lambda) \\ & + \mathsf{Adv}^{\mathsf{BadUniv}}_{\mathsf{VSHPS},\mathcal{B}}(1^\lambda). \end{split}$$

<span id="page-66-0"></span>**Lemma 5.** Games  $G_8$  and  $G_9$  are perfectly indistinguishable. That is, for any PPT adaptive adversary A, we have

$$\left| \Pr \left[ \boldsymbol{G}_{9}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1 \right] - \Pr \left[ \boldsymbol{G}_{8}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1 \right] \right| = 0,$$

*Proof.* We prove the lemma via a reduction from adaptive to selective security. The argument is structured in two parts, formalized in Lemma 6 and Lemma 3.

Lemma 6 establishes that no PPT selective adversary can distinguish between  $\mathbf{G}_8$  and  $\mathbf{G}_9$  with any advantage. Subsequently, by Lemma 3, we can extend the result to any PPT adaptive adversary  $\mathcal{A}$  that no PPT adaptive adversary  $\mathcal{A}$  can distinguish between  $\mathbf{G}_8$  and  $\mathbf{G}_9$  with any advantage which completes the proof.

<span id="page-66-1"></span>**Lemma 6.** For any PPT selective adversary  $\mathcal{B}$ , which by definition needs to commit to all its oracle queries before the game begins, we have:

$$\left| \Pr \left[ \mathbf{G}_9^{\mathcal{B}} \Rightarrow 1 \right] - \Pr \left[ \mathbf{G}_8^{\mathcal{B}} \Rightarrow 1 \right] \right| = 0.$$

Proof. We prove the lemma by introducing three intermediate games,  $G_{8.1}$ ,  $G_{8.2}$  and  $G_{8.3}$ , and show that for any selective adversary  $\mathcal{B}$ , the following chain of perfect indistinguishability holds:  $G_8 \approx_p G_{8.1} \approx_p G_{8.2} \approx_p G_{8.3} \approx_p G_9$ . This implies that  $G_8$  and  $G_9$  are perfectly indistinguishable for  $\mathcal{B}$ .

The simulation strategy for these games, detailed in Figure 22, leverages the selective nature of  $\mathcal{B}$ . Since all oracle queries are known beforehand, the challenger can simulate the environment without knowing most secret keys corresponding to challenge queries. Without loss of generality, we re-index users such that all challenge queries in  $\mathcal{L}_{\mathsf{C}}$  are for users  $i \in \{1, \ldots, |\mathsf{V}_{\mathsf{CL}}|\}$ .

Game  $G_{8.1}$ : This game, detailed in Figure 22, is identical to  $G_8$  but uses a different simulation strategy. The challenger first generates a key pair  $(hk_1, projk_1)$  and for each user  $i \in \{2, ..., |V_{CL}|\}$ , it generates  $projk_i := projk_1 + PKGen(d_{1,i}, \mathcal{L}_{lpk})$  via the re-encryption key  $d_{1,i}$ . Keys for non-challenge users  $i > |V_{CL}|$  are generated independently as in the original game. The challenger can answer all oracle queries using the known secret keys of non-challenge users and the re-encryption keys for challenge users.

The challenge ciphertext is generated using  $hk_1$  as in  $G_8$ . Since the distribution of keys and ciphertexts is identical to  $G_8$ , we have

$$|\mathsf{pr}_{8.1} - \mathsf{pr}_8| = 0.$$

{67}------------------------------------------------

```
Oracle \mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{CorrT}}(i,j):
Oracle \mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{KGen}}():
                                                                                                            15 if i, j \in \{1, ..., |V_{CL}|\}:
01 (lpk, td) \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} SMP.Setup(1^{\lambda}, \ell)
                                                                                                                         \mathbf{return} \ \mathsf{d}_{i,j} := \mathsf{d}_j - \mathsf{d}_i
                                                                                                            16
02 hk_1 \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} VSHPS.Setup(1^{\lambda})
                                                                                                            17 else
03 hk'_1 \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} VSHPS.Setup(1^{\lambda})
                                                                              G_{8.2-8.3}
                                                                        //
                                                                                                                          return d_{i,j} := hk_j - hk_i
                                                                                                            18
04 v \leftarrow U(\mathbb{F})
                                                                         /\!\!/ \mathbf{G}_{8.2-8.3}
05 hk_1 := hk'_1 + v \cdot h
                                                                        /\!\!/ \mathbf{G}_{8.2-8.3}
                                                                                                            Oracle \mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{CorrK}}(i):
06 \operatorname{projk}_1 \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \operatorname{PKGen}(\operatorname{hk}_1, \mathcal{L}_{\operatorname{lpk}})
                                                                       /\!\!/ \mathbf{G}_{8.1-8.2}
                                                                                                            19 if i \in \{|V_H| + 1, ..., N_K\}:
07 \operatorname{projk}_1 \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \operatorname{PKGen}(\operatorname{hk}_1', \mathcal{L}_{\operatorname{lpk}})
                                                                           \# \mathbf{G}_{8.3}
                                                                                                                          return hk_i
                                                                                                            20
08 for i \in \{2, ..., |V_{CL}|\}:
                                                                                                            21 return \perp
             d_i \leftarrow U(\mathcal{HK})
09
              \mathsf{projk}_i := \mathsf{projk}_1 + \mathsf{PKGen}(\mathsf{d}_i, \mathcal{L}_{\mathsf{lpk}})
10
11 d_1 = 0
12 for i \in \{|V_{CL}| + 1, \dots, N_K\}:
             \mathsf{hk}_i \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathsf{VSHPS}.\mathsf{Setup}(1^{\lambda})
13
14
              \mathsf{projk}_i := \mathsf{PKGen}(\mathsf{hk}_i, \mathcal{L}_{\mathsf{lpk}})
```

<span id="page-67-0"></span>Fig. 22. Description of the hybrid games  $G_{8.1}$ ,  $G_{8.2}$  and  $G_{8.3}$  in a selective adversary. The figure first show the difference between  $G_{8.1}$  under selective adversary and  $G_8$  under adaptive adversary. Then it illustrates the changes in the key generation process from  $G_{8.2}$  and  $G_{8.3}$ . Without loss of generality, we re-index keys such that challenge queries in  $\mathcal{L}_{C}$  correspond to the first  $|V_{CL}|$  users. The key generation oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{KGen}$  is executed only once at the start.

Game  $G_{8.2}$ : In this game, we modifies the generation of  $hk_1$ . Let  $h \in \mathcal{HK}''$  be a hash key such that  $SEval(h, ct_0) \neq 0$  for the challenge statement  $ct_0$ . Such an h is guaranteed to exist by the  $(\varepsilon, 1)$ -universality of the VSHPS. The challenger now computes  $hk_1 := hk'_1 + v \cdot h$ , where  $hk'_1 \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathcal{HK}$  and  $v \leftarrow U(\mathbb{F})$ . Since  $\mathcal{HK}$  is a vector space over  $\mathbb{F}$ , the distribution of  $hk_1$  remains uniform over  $\mathcal{HK}$ . Furthermore, by the definition of  $\mathcal{HK}''$ , we have  $PKGen(hk_1, \mathcal{L}_{lpk}) = PKGen(hk'_1, \mathcal{L}_{lpk})$ . Thus, the adversary's view is identical to that in  $G_{8.1}$ , and we have

$$|\mathsf{pr}_{8,2} - \mathsf{pr}_{8,1}| = 0.$$

Game  $G_{8.3}$ : This game modifies the generation of the projection key  $\operatorname{projk}_1$  by using the hash key  $\operatorname{hk}'_1$  instead of  $\operatorname{hk}_1$ . Moreover, we answer all the oracle queries except  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{Chall}}$  without knowing v, which is only used in the challenge ciphertext generation.

By the definition of  $\mathcal{HK}''$ , we have  $\mathsf{PKGen}(\mathsf{hk}_1, \mathcal{L}_{\mathsf{lpk}}) = \mathsf{PKGen}(\mathsf{hk}_1', \mathcal{L}_{\mathsf{lpk}})$ . Thus, the public key  $\mathsf{projk}_1$  remains unchanged. Since  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{CorrK}}$  is not queried for users  $i \in [|\mathsf{V}_{\mathsf{CL}}|]$ ,  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{CorrT}}$  queries for other challenged users  $i \in \{2, \cdots, |\mathsf{V}_{\mathsf{CL}}|\}$  are answered using  $\mathsf{d}_i$ , and for non-challenged users  $j > |\mathsf{V}_{\mathsf{CL}}|$ ,  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{CorrT}}$  queries are answered using their known secret keys, the adversary gets no information about  $\mathsf{hk}_1$  or  $\mathsf{hk}_1'$  from  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{CorrK}}$  and  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{CorrT}}$ . As for  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{REnc}}$  and  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{Dec}}$ , by the changes in  $G_5$  and  $G_6$ , the ciphertexts components  $\mathsf{ct}_0$  and  $\mathsf{ct}_1$  in the re-encryption queries and decryption queries are guaranteed to be in the language  $\mathcal{L}_{\mathsf{lpk}}$  with some witness.

{68}------------------------------------------------

Therefore, all the information the adversary can learn from these oracles is through the evaluation of  $SEval(hk_i - hk_1, ct_0)$  or  $SEval(hk_1, ct_0)$  for some users i. Since  $SEval(h, ct_0) = 0$ , We have  $SEval(hk_1, ct_0) = SEval(hk'_1, ct_0) + v \cdot SEval(hk, ct_0) = SEval(hk'_1, ct_0)$ , the answer remains unchanged. Therefore, the adversary's view in  $G_{8.2}$  and  $G_{8.3}$  is identical, leading to

$$pr_{8,3} = pr_{8,2}$$
.

In  $G_{8.3}$ , the challenge ciphertext component  $ct_1$  is computed as:

$$\mathsf{ct}_1 := \mathsf{SEval}(\mathsf{hk}_1' + v \cdot \mathsf{h}, \mathsf{ct}_0)$$

This is identical to the challenge ciphertext generation in  $G_9$ . The only difference lies in the generation of secret keys for users  $i \in \{2, \dots, |V_{CL}|\}$ . In  $G_{8.3}$ , these keys are implicitly defined as  $hk_i = hk'_1 + d_i$ , while in  $G_9$ , they are sampled uniformly from  $\mathcal{HK}$ . However, since  $d_i$  is uniformly random in  $\mathcal{HK}$  and independent of  $hk'_1$ , the distribution of  $hk'_i$  remains uniform over  $\mathcal{HK}$ . Thus, the distribution of all secret keys in both games is identical. Therefore, we have

$$pr_9 = pr_{8.3}$$
.

Combining the above results, we conclude that

$$\left| \Pr \left[ \mathbf{G}_9^{\mathcal{B}} \Rightarrow 1 \right] - \Pr \left[ \mathbf{G}_8^{\mathcal{B}} \Rightarrow 1 \right] \right| = 0.$$

## <span id="page-68-0"></span>H Security Proof for Multi-Challenge aCCA-Secure PRE

**Theorem 16.** If we instantiate the general construction of PRE<sub>aCCA</sub> Figure 6 with

- SMP: a hard subset membership language distribution
- VSHPS: a vector space hash proof system VSHPS with  $(\varepsilon, d)$ -universal, with  $d \ge k$ .
- OTS: an one-time signature scheme OTS that is one-time strongly unforgeable.
- tLM-NIZK: an one-time special simulation-sound tag-based language-malleable NIZK proof system tLM-NIZK for the language corresponded to SMP and VSHPS.

Then the resulting  $PRE_{aCCA}$  scheme is multi-challenge aCCA secure against any PPT adversary A, with advantage

$$\begin{split} \mathcal{A}_{\mathsf{PRE}_2,\mathcal{A}}^{\mathsf{aCCA},\mathsf{Q_C}}(\lambda) &= |\mathsf{pr}_0 - \mathsf{pr}_{14}| \leq \sum_{i=0}^{13} \left| \mathsf{pr}_i - \mathsf{pr}_{i+1} \right| \\ &\leq \binom{\mathsf{N_U}}{2} \cdot \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathsf{SMP},\mathcal{B}}^{\mathsf{KCol}}(1^\lambda) + \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathsf{tLM-NIZK},\mathcal{B}}^{\mathsf{ZK}}(1^\lambda) + \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathsf{OTS},\mathcal{B}}^{\mathsf{StUnforg}}(1^\lambda) \\ &+ \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathsf{H},\mathcal{B}}^{\mathsf{Collision}}(1^\lambda) + 2 \cdot \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathsf{tLM-NIZK},\mathcal{B}}^{\mathsf{SSS}}(1^\lambda) + 3 \cdot \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathsf{SMP},\mathcal{B}}^{\mathsf{HSM,Q_C}}(1^\lambda) \\ &+ \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathsf{VSHPS},\mathcal{B}}^{\mathsf{BadUniv}}(1^\lambda). \end{split}$$

{69}------------------------------------------------

*Proof.* The proof proceeds via a sequence of hybrid games,  $\mathbf{G}_0, \ldots, \mathbf{G}_{14}$ . The transitions from  $\mathbf{G}_0$  to  $\mathbf{G}_{10}$  mirror those in the proof of Theorem 15, but are adapted for the multi-challenge setting. The key differences are as follows:

- The transition from  $G_6$  to  $G_7$  relies on the  $Q_C$ -Hard Subset Membership ( $Q_C$ -HSM) property. All  $Q_C$  challenge statements are switched from being sampled in the language via  $\mathsf{Sample}_{\mathcal{L}}(\mathsf{lpk})$  to being sampled uniformly from the ambient space via  $\mathsf{Sample}_{\mathcal{L}}(1^{\lambda})$ . This introduces a difference of at most  $\mathsf{Adv}_{\mathsf{SMP},\mathcal{B}}^{\mathsf{HSM},Q_C}(1^{\lambda})$ .
- In  $G_8$ , the bad event  $\mathsf{Bad}_{\mathsf{Univ}}$  is defined with respect to the  $(\varepsilon, d)$ -universality of the VSHPS. The difference is bounded by  $|\mathsf{pr}_8 \mathsf{pr}_7| \leq \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathsf{VSHPS},\mathcal{B}}^{\mathsf{Bad}\mathsf{Univ}}(1^{\lambda})$ .
- In  $\mathbf{G}_9$  and  $\mathbf{G}_{10}$ , the challenge ciphertext is randomized. Let  $\mathbf{H} \in \mathbb{F}^{d \times \ell}$  be a basis of the  $\mathcal{HK}''$  over linear language  $\mathcal{L}_{\mathsf{lpk}}$ . We sample random vectors  $\mathbf{v}, \mathbf{v}' \in \mathbb{F}^d$  and compute the challenge ciphertext as  $\mathsf{ct}_1^j := \mathsf{SEval}(\mathsf{hk}_i + \mathbf{v}^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{H} + \mathsf{hk}, \mathsf{ct}_0^j)$  and  $\mathsf{ct}_2^j := \mathsf{SEval}(\mathsf{hk} + \mathbf{v}'\mathbf{H}, \mathsf{ct}_0^j) + \mathsf{m}_b^j$  for  $j \in [\mathsf{Q}_\mathsf{C}]$  and  $i \in [\mathsf{N}_\mathsf{U}]$  indexing the challenge users. The proof of this step is similar to the single-challenge case, but requires a more detailed explanation.
  - In  $G_{8.1}$ , we index the first challenge user as 1 and generate its secret key  $hk_1$  normally. We add a relative token  $d_i$  for each other challenge user  $i^{23}$ , so we can still simulate all the oracle queries perfectly without knowing any other user's secret key in list  $V_{CL}$ .
  - In  $G_{8.2}$  and  $G_{8.3}$ , we do the same modification as in the single-challenge case, except that we now sample a random vector  $\mathbf{v} \in \mathbb{F}^d$  and compute  $\mathsf{hk}_1 := \mathsf{hk}_1' + \mathbf{v}^\intercal \cdot \mathbf{H}$ , where  $\mathsf{hk}_1' \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathcal{HK}$ . We note that since all the challenge users share the same hash key  $\mathsf{hk}_1$ , the random vector  $\mathbf{v}^\intercal \mathbf{H}$  is also shared among all challenge ciphertexts.
  - In  $G_{10}$ , since all the challenge ciphertexts share the same hash key hk, the random vector  $\mathbf{v}'\mathbf{H}$  is also shared among all challenge ciphertexts.

As in the single-challenge case, this change is purely conceptual, so we have  $pr_9 = pr_8$  and  $pr_{10} = pr_9$ .

The subsequent games,  $G_{11}$  through  $G_{14}$ , are detailed in Figure 9 and complete the reduction.

<u>Game  $G_{11}$ :</u> In this game, we change the distribution of the statement component  $ct_0$  for all challenge ciphertexts. Instead of sampling  $ct_0$  uniformly from the ambient space via  $\mathsf{Sample}_{\mathcal{L}}(1^{\lambda})$ , we sample it from the language  $\mathcal{L}_{\mathsf{lpk}_1}$  via  $\mathsf{Sample}_{\mathcal{L}}(\mathsf{lpk}_1)$ , where  $\mathsf{lpk}_1 \stackrel{\hspace{0.1em}\mathsf{\scriptscriptstyle\$}}{\leftarrow} \mathsf{SMP}.\mathsf{Setup}(1^{\lambda},\ell)$  is new language public key. The difference between  $G_{10}$  and  $G_{11}$  is bounded by the  $\mathsf{Q}_\mathsf{C}\text{-HSM}$  property of the language.

$$|\mathsf{pr}_{11} - \mathsf{pr}_{10}| \leq \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathsf{SMP},\mathcal{B}}^{\mathsf{HSM},\mathsf{Q}_{\mathsf{C}}}(1^{\lambda}).$$

Game  $G_{12}$ : This game is a conceptual rewrite of  $G_{11}$ . Since  $ct_2$  is similar to  $ct_1$ , we only explain the change for  $ct_1$ .

<span id="page-69-0"></span>The adversary may not queries a  $\mathcal{O}_{CorrT}$  between two challenge users which make the graph of  $V_{CL}$  is not connected

{70}------------------------------------------------

$$\begin{array}{c|ccccccccccccccccccccccccccccccccccc$$

Fig. 23. Hybrid games for aCCA security from  $G_9$  onwards.

We first express the challenge ciphertext generation in matrix form, which does not change the adversary's view. Then we rewrite the term  $\mathsf{SEval}(\mathbf{v}^\intercal\mathbf{H},\mathsf{x})$  as  $\mathbf{R}^\intercal \cdot \mathsf{x}$  where  $\mathbf{R}^\intercal := \mathsf{SEval}(\mathbf{v}^\intercal\mathbf{H}, \mathbf{u}_1)| \cdots | \mathsf{SEval}(\mathbf{v}^\intercal\mathbf{H}, \mathbf{u}_\ell)$  is a row vector in  $\mathbb{F}^{1 \times \ell}$  and  $\mathbf{u}_1, \ldots, \mathbf{u}_\ell$  is the standard basis of  $\mathbb{F}^\ell$ . Since  $\mathsf{SEval}$  is linear in its second argument, we have  $\mathsf{SEval}(\mathbf{v}^\intercal\mathbf{H}, \mathsf{x}) = \mathbf{R}^\intercal \cdot \mathsf{x}$ . Finally, we modify the vector  $\mathbf{R}$  to be uniformly random in a subspace of dimension d of  $\mathbb{F}^{\ell \times 1}$ , where d is the dimension of the hash key space  $\mathcal{HK}''$ . This change is valid because  $\mathbf{v} \in \mathbb{F}^d$  is uniformly random,  $\mathbf{H} \in \mathbb{F}^{d \times \ell}$  has full row rank d, and the vectors  $\mathbf{u}_1, \ldots, \mathbf{u}_\ell$  are linearly independent. By the d-MinEntropy property of VSHPS,  $\mathbf{R}$  has full min-entropy  $d \cdot \log |\mathbb{F}|$ . Thus we can rewrite  $\mathbf{R}$  as  $\mathbf{r}^\intercal\mathbf{M} + \mathbf{R}_0$  for some fixed  $\mathbf{R}_0 \in \mathbb{F}^{\ell \times 1}$ , where  $\mathbf{r} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathsf{U}(\mathbb{F}^d)$  and  $\mathbf{M} \in \mathbb{F}^{d \times \ell}$  is a full row rank matrix, the change is purely conceptual.

Thus, the games are perfectly indistinguishable, we have

$$|\mathsf{pr}_{12} - \mathsf{pr}_{11}| = 0$$

**Game G**<sub>13</sub>: This game reinterprets the structure of the challenge ciphertext.

In  $\mathbf{G}_{11}$ , the vector added to the core encryption is  $\begin{pmatrix} \mathbf{x} \\ \mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{M} \cdot \mathbf{x} \end{pmatrix} = \begin{pmatrix} \mathbf{I}_{\ell} \\ \mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{M} \end{pmatrix} \cdot \mathbf{x}$ . Since  $\mathbf{I}_{\ell}$  is the  $\ell \times \ell$  identity matrix,  $\mathbf{r}$  and  $\mathbf{r}'$  are random vectors in  $\mathbb{F}^d$  with  $d \geq k = dim(\mathcal{L}_{\mathsf{lpk}_1})$  and  $\mathbf{M} \in \mathbb{F}^{d \times \ell}$  is a full row rank matrix, the matrix  $\begin{pmatrix} \mathbf{I}_{\ell} \\ \mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{M} \end{pmatrix}$ 

is a isomorphism from  $\mathcal{L}_{\mathsf{lpk}_1}$  to a new linear space of dimension k over an ambient

{71}------------------------------------------------

space of dimension  $\ell+2$ . We denote this new linear space as  $\mathcal{L}_{\mathsf{lpk}'_1}$ , and rewrite the

$$\text{challenge ciphertexts as} \begin{pmatrix} \mathsf{ct}_0 \\ \mathsf{ct}_1 \\ \mathsf{ct}_2 \end{pmatrix} := \begin{pmatrix} \mathbf{0} \\ \mathsf{SEval}(\mathsf{hk}_i, \bar{\mathsf{x'}}) + \mathbf{R}_0^\mathsf{T} \cdot \bar{\mathsf{x'}} \\ \mathsf{SEval}(\mathsf{hk}, \bar{\mathsf{x'}}) + \mathsf{m}_b + \mathbf{R}_0^{\mathsf{T}} \cdot \bar{\mathsf{x'}} \end{pmatrix} + \mathsf{x'}, \text{ where }$$

 $(x', w) \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathsf{Sample}_{\mathcal{L}}(\mathsf{Ipk}_1') \text{ and } x' \text{ is the first } \ell \text{ components of } x'.$ 

This change is purely conceptual, so the games are perfectly indistinguishable, we have

$$pr_{13} = pr_{12}$$
.

Game  $G_{14}$ : In this final game, we change how x' is generated for all challenge ciphertexts. Instead of sampling x' from the language  $\mathcal{L}_{lpk'_1}$  via  $\mathsf{Sample}_{\mathcal{L}}(lpk'_1)$ , we sample it uniformly at random from the ambient space  $\mathbb{F}^{\ell+2}$  via  $\mathsf{Sample}_{\mathcal{L}}(1^{\lambda})$ . The indistinguishability between  $G_{13}$  and  $G_{14}$  is guaranteed by the  $\mathsf{Q}_\mathsf{C}\text{-HSM}$  property of the language  $\mathcal{L}_{lpk'_1}$ .

$$|\mathsf{pr}_{14} - \mathsf{pr}_{13}| \leq \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathsf{SMP},\mathcal{B}}^{\mathsf{HSM},\mathsf{Q}_{\mathsf{C}}}(1^{\lambda}).$$

In  $G_{14}$ , by the above game transitions, the challenge ciphertexts is computed

as 
$$\begin{pmatrix} \mathsf{ct}_0 \\ \mathsf{ct}_1 \\ \mathsf{ct}_2 \end{pmatrix} := \begin{pmatrix} \mathbf{0} \\ \mathsf{SEval}(\mathsf{hk}_i + \mathsf{hk}, \bar{\mathsf{x'}}) + \mathbf{R}_0^\mathsf{T} \cdot \bar{\mathsf{x'}} \\ \mathsf{SEval}(\mathsf{hk}, \bar{\mathsf{x'}}) + \mathsf{m}_b + \mathbf{R}_0'^\mathsf{T} \cdot \bar{\mathsf{x'}} \end{pmatrix} + \mathsf{x'}, \text{ where } \mathsf{x'} \text{ is a uniformly random}$$

vector in  $\mathbb{F}^{\ell+2}$ . This vector acts as a one-time pad, making the resulting ciphertext  $(\mathsf{ct}_0, \mathsf{ct}_1, \mathsf{ct}_2)$  uniformly random and statistically independent of the challenge bit b. Consequently, the adversary's advantage is zero.

$$\operatorname{pr}_{14}=\frac{1}{2}.$$

Combining the bounds from all game transitions yields the final security advantage:

$$\begin{split} \mathcal{A}_{\mathsf{PRE}_2,\mathcal{A}}^{\mathsf{aCCA},\mathsf{Q_C}}(\lambda) &= |\mathsf{pr}_0 - \mathsf{pr}_{14}| \leq \sum_{i=0}^{13} \left| \mathsf{pr}_i - \mathsf{pr}_{i+1} \right| \\ &\leq \binom{\mathsf{N_U}}{2} \cdot \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathsf{SMP},\mathcal{B}}^{\mathsf{KCol}}(1^\lambda) + \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathsf{tLM-NIZK},\mathcal{B}}^{\mathsf{ZK}}(1^\lambda) + \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathsf{OTS},\mathcal{B}}^{\mathsf{StUnforg}}(1^\lambda) \\ &+ \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathsf{H},\mathcal{B}}^{\mathsf{Collision}}(1^\lambda) + 2 \cdot \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathsf{tLM-NIZK},\mathcal{B}}^{\mathsf{SSS}}(1^\lambda) + 3 \cdot \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathsf{SMP},\mathcal{B}}^{\mathsf{HSM},\mathsf{Q_C}}(1^\lambda) \\ &+ \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathsf{VSHPS},\mathcal{B}}^{\mathsf{BadUniv}}(1^\lambda). \end{split}$$
